  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f93ebb68-ac6a-4626-8ffb-f21997198d99'
      });

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1889715934" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1889715934" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7383561-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374678939p2/7383561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1889715934?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/7383561-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7383561-holly?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1889715934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15694806008178848055"><b>
  <u>Why I think this book was, quite frankly, terrible:</u>
</b><br/>- It's set in the 19th century yet the speech and thoughts used by the characters are very modern and quite out of time/place<br/><br/>- The heroine is supposedly a "feminist" which, according to this book, means she must hate and/or resent all men. A man wrote this book? You don't say!<br/><br/>- A major part of the plot is that Lilly, a female, takes on a male persona in order to work for Mr. Ambrose. This is not a deception, he knows the whole time that she </span>
  <span id="freeText15694806008178848055" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Why I think this book was, quite frankly, terrible:</u>
</b><br />- It's set in the 19th century yet the speech and thoughts used by the characters are very modern and quite out of time/place<br /><br />- The heroine is supposedly a "feminist" which, according to this book, means she must hate and/or resent all men. A man wrote this book? You don't say!<br /><br />- A major part of the plot is that Lilly, a female, takes on a male persona in order to work for Mr. Ambrose. This is not a deception, he knows the whole time that she is a female and yet he still consistently calls her by her fake male name, even in private. It's weird.<br /><br />- There's basically no actual romance in this book. So despite the fact that this book was listed in the romance category of the Goodreads Choice Awards, don't read this entire book waiting and waiting for romance to eventually become a part of the plot because you are going to be very disappointed.<br /><br />- There are several chapters that are not about the main protagonists and they are <b>BORING BEYOND BELIEF AND NEVER ENDING</b>. No, seriously. Even positive reviews for this book repeatedly mention how these chapters are the worst. <br /><br />- You may notice that all the chapters tend to end in a cliffhanger-ish way, and that would be because this book was written and released one chapter at a time on a website called wattpad, where you can still read this book in it's entirety for free<br /><br />- Speaking of wattpad, since it was originally published on that site, this book has not been professionally edited in any way, shape, or form. So lower your expectations accordingly. A lack of editing is not always a terrible thing, I do love some indie authors who do not have editors, but it is definitely a bad thing for this book in particular. It could have been cut in half easily and you would have lost nothing of substance.<br /><br />- If you manage to successfully struggle through reading this entire (way, way too long because it wasn't edited) book you are treated with an ending that is basically <b>a rip off of the Titanic</b>. I am not even making that up. <br /><br /><br /><b>So, if you really want to read a romance novel in a historical setting that isn't believably set in historic times and also does not actually involve any romance, then this is the book for you!</b> Otherwise, you might want to give this book a pass.<br /><br />This book has an <b>
  <u>OBSCENELY INFLATED AVERAGE RATING</u>
</b>. I would love to show you receipts proving that it's inflated, and was not entirely the result of actual individual people rating this book so highly, but I can't because unfortunately when I previously did that, <b>
  <u>Goodreads deleted my review</u>
</b> because apparently it's a violation of "review guidelines". They deleted my review twice now, in fact. <br /><br />Why did they delete my review the second time? Because it turns out I can't even tell you in the comments section what happened because, per Goodreads's email to me: <i>"...attempting to circumvent our review guidelines by posting the text of the review in the comments also violates our rules." </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15694806008178848055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3815269359674524620">One of the best books on Wattpad. It is historical fiction and takes place in London when women couldn't vote or do anything really. It follows Lilly Linton as she gets the opportunity to get a job...so long as she is dressed like a man. Her and her boss (Rikkard Ambrose) must learn to deal with each other and you can feel the connection between them even if she (a feminist) goes out of her way to deny ever wanting to be married and getting stuck as a housewife and he (a brooding money saving mi</span>
  <span id="freeText3815269359674524620" style="display:none">One of the best books on Wattpad. It is historical fiction and takes place in London when women couldn't vote or do anything really. It follows Lilly Linton as she gets the opportunity to get a job...so long as she is dressed like a man. Her and her boss (Rikkard Ambrose) must learn to deal with each other and you can feel the connection between them even if she (a feminist) goes out of her way to deny ever wanting to be married and getting stuck as a housewife and he (a brooding money saving millionaire) tries to get rid of her any way he can. I love love love this book, it gets updated every Wednesday and hopefully one day it will get published and I can buy it, Robert Thier interacts with his fans and is just a great guy all around and his English is remarkable for someone who doesn't speak English as a first language. READ IT </span>

<div id="review_1582623151" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582623151" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582623151?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582623151" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7265585403896267250"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Chains of gold are still chains.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>After I finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24035804.Storm_and_Silence__Storm_and_Silence___1_' title='Storm and Silence (Storm and Silence, #1) by Robert Thier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Storm and Silence</a> last night I was overwhelmed with so many different and powerful feelings that I could not utter a single sentence that made sense. And now I've been staring at my computer screen for hours and I don't know what to type. It's kind of disorienting people. Just like the book's finale.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447559239ra/17021797.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>What's the story?</u>
</b><br/><b>Victorian era, balls, politics, mystery, slow burning romance and a brooding and rude male lead</b>, I could not possib</span>
  <span id="freeText7265585403896267250" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Chains of gold are still chains.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>After I finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24035804.Storm_and_Silence__Storm_and_Silence___1_" title="Storm and Silence (Storm and Silence, #1) by Robert Thier" rel="nofollow noopener">Storm and Silence</a> last night I was overwhelmed with so many different and powerful feelings that I could not utter a single sentence that made sense. And now I've been staring at my computer screen for hours and I don't know what to type. It's kind of disorienting people. Just like the book's finale.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447559239ra/17021797.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>What's the story?</u>
</b><br><b>Victorian era, balls, politics, mystery, slow burning romance and a brooding and rude male lead</b>, I could not possibly ask for more! Lilly Linton is not your typical lady, her story begins when she tries (and fails) to vote in the elections because she strongly believes in gender equality and despises the idea that a woman's place is at home, giving birth to a horde of children, always ruled and overshadowed by her master and husband. She craves freedom and independence, and when she accidentally lands a job as a secretary to the most powerful man in the British Empire, she thinks her future is bright. But Mr Ambrose is a stubborn and infuriating chauvinist who can't stand her and enjoys torturing her. When a document of value is stolen from his possession, Lilly finds herself in the middle of a dangerous vendetta and the events that follow endanger her position, her life, her ideals and worst of all, her heart.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Life is not about living the safer option. Life is about living a life worth living.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Pros</u>
</b><br>➺ The narrative was extremely <b>amusing</b>, full of <b>snarky</b> inner dialogues and witty banters that made me chuckle countless times!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“So we have one more thing on our to-do list. Achieve women's suffrage and get the inventor of solid chocolate bars knighted for his achievements.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➺ It gave me plenty <b>food for thought</b>. Every day I wake up, attend college, study, engage in political conversations and it is totally normal, something as certain and expected as breathing. I forget how many hardships women endured through the ages so that I can take everything for granted, how many sacrifices and battles took place so that I can proudly claim that I am equal to any man, that I have the same rights and responsibilities. Lilly's fights reminded me of that and I am truly grateful.<br>➺ The <b>mystery</b>, while it unfolded slowly, set the bases for some gripping last chapters and agonizing, nail-biting moments!<br>➺ <b>I am quite enamored with Mr Ambrose</b>! The man was the world's biggest miser, with an easy temper and and zero tolerance to anyone who opposed him, but I was enchanted by his rare protective, considerate and vulnerable moments. His harsh lines and rude manners just added to his allure!<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A man.<br>A really manly man with a lot of mannishness in his manliness.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>➺ The <b>romance</b> was building slowly but steadily, you could feel the tension and the fruitless struggle for control oozing from both Lilly and Mr Ambrose, but alas! they came to find that the heart does not follow what the mind dictates, it sets its own path and burns the readers with anticipation in the process!<br><br><b>
  <u>Cons</u>
</b><br>➺ There were parts where <b>the story dragged on and could be tiring</b>. Some scenes were longer than they should and I would have enjoyed it more if it was 100-200 pages shorter.<br>➺ Lilly could be really <b>annoying</b> at times, she had some traits I admired but she could also be so darn naive, childish and stubborn when she shouldn't! Following orders is not always a bad thing, especially when they try to save your life, girl! And being a feminist doesn't mean you can't develop feelings for a man! Gosh I wanted to talk some sense into her thick skull!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458339530ra/18476220.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But nothing mattered after that <b>jaw-dropping end</b>! Congratulations Mr Thier, I had a heart attack and now I can't wait to get the second books in my hands!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/420316.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*Free copy generously provided by the author in exchange for an honest review*</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7265585403896267250" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1530492409" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1530492409" />
    <a title="Pam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13865261-pam"><img alt="Pam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374039144p2/13865261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1530492409?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pam" href="/user/show/13865261-pam">Pam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28502955-storm-and-silence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=4">4</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=sweeter-side">sweeter-side</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13865261-pam?shelf=mystery-kinda-luv">mystery-kinda-luv</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1530492409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10737932070503818227"><i>4.25 ‘My little Ifrit,’ stars</i><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘Knowledge is power is time is money!’ </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459143110ra/18573639.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>What does <i>a suffragette and a chauvinist,</i> have in common ???? Absolutely nothing, BUT it makes for great entertaining reading. I enjoyed this in it's entirety, because it had a little bit of everything that kept me engaged throughout it's 885 pages. It is LONG, but it's also very well written that it makes the pages just fly by. <br/><br/><b>Lilly Linton aka Mr. Linton</b> wants nothing more than her freedom, to do as she pleases and</span>
  <span id="freeText10737932070503818227" style="display:none"><i>4.25 ‘My little Ifrit,’ stars</i><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘Knowledge is power is time is money!’ </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459143110ra/18573639.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>What does <i>a suffragette and a chauvinist,</i> have in common ???? Absolutely nothing, BUT it makes for great entertaining reading. I enjoyed this in it's entirety, because it had a little bit of everything that kept me engaged throughout it's 885 pages. It is LONG, but it's also very well written that it makes the pages just fly by. <br><br><b>Lilly Linton aka Mr. Linton</b> wants nothing more than her freedom, to do as she pleases and provide for herself. She does not want to rely on a marriage to want for nothing, that is just simply moving from one prison to another. She wants to be an equal, recognized and respected; she just never thought that she would get all that only if she dressed as a <i>man.</i> She finds her chance in <b>Mr. Ambrose</b>, a most infuriating and mysterious man, who she hasn't decided yet if she wants to strangle or hug...after all he is the man who will pay her wages. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I remain Sincerely Yours Miss Lilly Linton<br>.............................................................<br>And incidentally, I do not want you as mine, sincerely or otherwise. Rikkard Ambrose<br>.............................................................<br>Yours (as your secretary, whether you like it or not) Lilly Linton</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Lucky for Lilly, the feeling is mutual, if he hadn't given her his word, this would be a mute discussion, however he is a man who means what he says. To bad for him she refuses to do as she is told, finding every loophole manageable, knowing when to argue and purposely disobeying ever command he decrees. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‘You know, Mr Linton, you have a way of saying “Sir” that makes it sound astonishingly like a synonym for “miserable chauvinist worm”.’<br><br>‘I wonder why that is.’ </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>On top of Lily's ongoing campaign for women's rights, she has to find a way to save her younger sister form a arranged betrothal, she sets her plan in motion to make Mr. Ambrose see reason to need her as much as she needs him.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Yours always (Which means you’re not getting rid of me!) Miss Lilly Linton </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1459143110ra/18573640.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Storm and Silence</b> is a PG-rated book that I had fun with, it was witty, funny, and enlightening. Although this took place in the past, it was written in a way that can be enjoyed by everyone. Their banter, their frustration, their stubbornness with each other is the main reason that I enjoyed this book. It really had a little of everything, we got the sweet love story from Lilly's younger sister, some spy action and a look into how limited women's rights were. Now my only complaint is the ending, in a way I am glad there will be more, but the cliff hanger left me literally with my mouth hanging open. Suffice to say, I do recommend this read for those who can appreciate the journey and not rush towards a destination. I can't wait for the next one!<br><br><i>ARC kindly provided by the author, in exchange for an honest review.</i><br> <br>***Quotes above are taken from the ARC version of the book and may differ upon publication.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10737932070503818227" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer391671380854671893"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Great. Now I’m hooked on historical romance. Something I thought would NEVER happen.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418505.gif' width='500"/' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>You see, I’m not a fan of historical romance. The reason is pretty simple.<br/><br/>Ever been forced by your teachers to read Sophocles’ Antigone, Homer's Iliad and Odyssey or Dante’s Divine Comedy at the age of fifteen?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418506.gif' width='500"/' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>So history in my leisure time? Yeahno...<br/><br/>Still, I picked up this book because of two reasons: First, it made the finals of the Goodreads Choice Awards this year. Second, I read that the hero was a</span>
  <span id="freeText391671380854671893" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br><br>Great. Now I’m hooked on historical romance. Something I thought would NEVER happen.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418505.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>You see, I’m not a fan of historical romance. The reason is pretty simple.<br><br>Ever been forced by your teachers to read Sophocles’ Antigone, Homer's Iliad and Odyssey or Dante’s Divine Comedy at the age of fifteen?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418506.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So history in my leisure time? Yeahno...<br><br>Still, I picked up this book because of two reasons: First, it made the finals of the Goodreads Choice Awards this year. Second, I read that the hero was a cold, stoic jerk. My favorite.<br><br>Ladies and gents, meet <b>Mr Rikkard Ambrose</b>...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418508.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Honorable, moral, mysterious, broody, unreachable, disinterested, impolite, stingy, randomly considerate, forbidding, reserved, stony, distant, taciturn and cold as the North Pole. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>A moment later, the door opened and he stood before me: Mr Rikkard Ambrose in all his cold, stony glory. His eyes were like dark pools of unfathomable deep water. His mouth could have been carved from granite. And his lips…<br><br>He seemed to radiate negative noise.</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418509.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br>The words that come out of his mouth ... <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Mr Linton,<br>Please correct your address of me to coincide with the truth. I am not ‘dear’ to anyone, least of all, I am sure, to you. Also, it is my ink you are wasting by writing unnecessary words. A bottle of ink costs 3 pence apiece. Therefore, I order you to refrain from all endearments in the future.<br><br>‘Mr Linton?’<br>‘I can feel your smile. Dispose of it immediately.’<br><br>I waved my arms, making the uniform stretch uncomfortably. ‘The uniform is rather tight over my other clothes.’<br>‘It may surprise you to hear this, Mr Linton, but I do not care. This is not a Paris fashion show.’<br><br>‘N-no, Sir. I simply find it rather hot in here. Don’t you, Sir?’<br>‘To be absolutely accurate, I could not care less about the climatic conditions in here, Mr Linton.’</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418511.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418512.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>"Mr" Linton...</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481394102i/21418519._SY540_.jpg" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>A woman disguised as a man in order to fight for women’s suffrage. An insufferable nuisance to every man. One of the most badass heroines in the literature.<br><br>I love love her personality! She has a stormy temperament and she’s independent, fierce, passionate, rebellious, adventurous, courageous, loyal, persistent and sassy. <br><br>And although she wants to do with her life more 'than exist as an appendix to some chauvinist blockhead', she can’t resist falling for His Mightiness, Ambrose the Icy. <br><br>Who could, anyway?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418522.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>This book was so freaking good. I can’t remember the last time I laughed so hard. <br><br>Some things were a bit unrealistic and some scenes seemed silly and over the top but Mr. Thier’s writing is so refreshing and so full of sarcasm, wit and personality that you can’t help but fall in love with his style, with this adventurous, mysterious and suspenseful story and amazingly well-developed characters. <br><br>Oh, and just to be clear...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1481394102ra/21418523.gif" width='500"/' class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><b>Enjoyment:</b>: 4.5/5<br><b>Writing style:</b> 5/5<br><b>Storyline:</b> 5/5<br><b>Hero:</b> 5/5 <br><b>Heroine:</b> 5/5<br><b>Secondary characters:</b> 5/5 <br><b>Hotness/chemistry:</b> 4/5 <br><b>Romance:</b> 4/5 <br><b>Angst:</b> 3/5<br><b>Darkness level:</b> 3/5<br><b>Humor:</b> 5/5<br><b> Depth of the book:</b> 5/5<br><b>POV:</b> heroine, 1st person<br><b> Triggers:</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view   <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1519550086" />
    <a title="Jaidee " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295672-jaidee"><img alt="Jaidee " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558439086p2/17295672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1519550086?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jaidee " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jaidee " href="/user/show/17295672-jaidee">Jaidee </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">sweet young feminists battling their hormonal urges</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jaidee  by: </span>
      Mr. Thier approached me.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295672-jaidee?shelf=three-stars-books">three-stars-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1519550086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1011887331797993688">3 "Cinder(f)ella meets Nancy Drew meets James Bond meets musical theatre" stars !!!<br/><br/><b> 2016 Book Where I Wished I Was Editor </b><br/><br/>Please note I received a complimentary e-book from the author in exchange for a book review.<br/><br/>First of all I want to say I am really excited to be writing this review! Many of my 3-star reviews are tinged with disappointment of what "could have been amazing" where with this book I have so much hope that it can reach its full potential and become a 4 or even 4.5 star young adult</span>
  <span id="freeText1011887331797993688" style="display:none">3 "Cinder(f)ella meets Nancy Drew meets James Bond meets musical theatre" stars !!!<br /><br /><b> 2016 Book Where I Wished I Was Editor </b><br /><br />Please note I received a complimentary e-book from the author in exchange for a book review.<br /><br />First of all I want to say I am really excited to be writing this review! Many of my 3-star reviews are tinged with disappointment of what "could have been amazing" where with this book I have so much hope that it can reach its full potential and become a 4 or even 4.5 star young adult read.<br /><br />This book won the 2015 people's choice Watty award on Wattpad. I had not heard of this website (can you believe it? - of course you can) and has received millions of reads and votes. This is phenomenal and well-deserved. The book is to be published I believe in March 2016 due to its immense popularity.<br /><br />I am very happy and excited for Mr. Thier or Sir Rob as his fans call him.<br /><br />Not since reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17333223.The_Goldfinch" title="The Goldfinch by Donna Tartt" rel="nofollow noopener">The Goldfinch</a> have I itched to be a book editor (soooo bad). I want to make this "good" book a "phenomenal" book as it has all the elements in it to be so. I hope I do not sound too pompous when I say this as there were many moments when I enjoyed this book immensely and others where I wanted to pull my hair out.<br /><br />Let's start with what I LOVED in this romantic comedy adventure:<br /><br />1. the overall story arc was exciting, sweet, fun, clean, and lovely.<br />2. Lilly and Rikkard (the reluctant lovebirds) were a wonderful match. Lilly was fun, feisty, principled and downright adorable. Rikkard was smouldering, sexy, powerful, intelligent and even caring. They were both such dynamic and interesting characters.<br />3. some sweet melodramatic subplots (Ella and Edmund, the suffragettes etc.)<br />4. the internal conflict between Lilly's feminist principles and the fire that is triggered in heterosexual desire.<br />5. this could be turned into a really amazing family musical (in fact in my mind's eye all I saw was singing, dancing, acrobatics) I would give Chillina Kennedy the role of Lilly and I'm still pondering who I would give the role of Rikkard to. Does anybody know if Ryan Reynolds can sing?<br /><br />What I HATED (so sorry to his fans). I feel sooooo strongly that the following detracted HUGELY from what could make this YA book almost perfect.<br /><br />1. the length....this went on for way too long for the amount of story....I could easily cut out a third of this book.....very repetitive at times.<br />2. the amount of humor was EXCESSIVE....way toooooo much of it....rather than make me laugh it would often make me faux-angry as it detracted from the adventure or sweetness or both. Some the humor was very funny but some of it (sorry Sir Rob) was just plain awful and I mean awful.<br />3. the repetitiveness of many of the adjectives.....some of them I swear were used upwards of a hundred times. This annoyed the hell out of me.<br />4. I also felt that many of Lilly's thought patterns were extremely anachronistic as was the use of some the language. This could be very jarring to the reader...well this reader anyway.<br /><br />I want to end off by saying that what comes through in spades is:<br /><br />A lovely light spirited novel where the conflict between principles, beliefs, dogmas is juxtaposed with the human desire for love, belonging and a little bit of passion and adventure.<br /><br />Kudos to you Sir Rob. I wish you the very best in your writing endeavors<br /><br />Now if you need anybody to help you write lyrics for the musical....you know where to find me ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1011887331797993688" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1527422131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14674799069798410656"><b> Ebook copy kindly provided by the author in exchange for an honest review. Thank you so much. </b><br/><br/>Gah. This book. Where do I even start? <br/><br/>If you're a Jane Austen fan, drop everything and go pick up this book. You won't regret it, I promise.<br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424689665ra/13791594.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I have a strong suspicion that Robert Thier is actually a descendant of Jane Austen somehow. I can't prove it but there's no other possible explanation. <br/><br/>Here's what you can expect from this book: <br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458157811ra/18451348.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>➨ Miss Lilly Linton AKA Mr Linton is not your typical Victorian pe</span>
  <span id="freeText14674799069798410656" style="display:none"><b> Ebook copy kindly provided by the author in exchange for an honest review. Thank you so much. </b><br><br>Gah. This book. Where do I even start? <br><br>If you're a Jane Austen fan, drop everything and go pick up this book. You won't regret it, I promise.<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1424689665ra/13791594.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I have a strong suspicion that Robert Thier is actually a descendant of Jane Austen somehow. I can't prove it but there's no other possible explanation. <br><br>Here's what you can expect from this book: <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458157811ra/18451348.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>➨ Miss Lilly Linton AKA Mr Linton is not your typical Victorian period female character. She is a feminist young girl who wants to get the right to vote for women and the right to work in order to provide for herself without having to rely on anyone else. Obviously, these things were not possible at that time so she gets herself in all sorts of shenanigans. <br><br>➨Mr Rikkard Ambrose: *cough* Mr Darcy *cough* <br>I have to admit Mr Ambrose acts like a complete jerk throughout the majority of the book but we can't help but love him. I think it's the blue eyes. *fans self* <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447291298ra/16981870.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>➨An entertaining journey: If I could describe this book in just one word it would be "entertaining" you can just forget about everything that's bugging you in your life and have a fun time reading this book. <br><br>A few things I didn't enjoy about this book:<br><br>➨The cover: <br>It doesn't rightfully reflect the vibe of the book. To be honest, when I look at it I expect some new adult/erotic novel while in fact it is a young adult historical fiction so don't be fooled by the cover. <br><br>➨The length: <br>The book was a little too big for my taste, I felt like some parts could have been cut out without harming the book but that's just my opinion. <br><br>Overall, I honestly believe that this book would appeal to a variety of people, you don't really have to be into this genre in order to enjoy this book. Highly recommend it to you guys. <br><br>Thanks for reading. Share your thoughts. <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="14674799069798410656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1520517703" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520517703" />
    <a title="BookLover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12285159-booklover"><img alt="BookLover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459818210p2/12285159.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520517703?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BookLover" href="/user/show/12285159-booklover">BookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=arc-netgalley">arc-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=rs">rs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=tpl">tpl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=author-first-reads">author-first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12285159-booklover?shelf=favourite-authors">favourite-authors</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520517703" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4434355443695579499"><i>ARC provided by the author in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>After receiving a request from the author to read and review this book, I read the description, saw all of the positive reviews and decided to give it a go. I love historical fiction and wasn’t sure what to expect with this story.<br/><br/>My first reaction when I opened the book up after receiving it? Holy sh*% this is a long book. I’m talking Outlander long. Luckily, a long book does not scare me off. My second reaction after reading the first </span>
  <span id="freeText4434355443695579499" style="display:none"><i>ARC provided by the author in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br>After receiving a request from the author to read and review this book, I read the description, saw all of the positive reviews and decided to give it a go. I love historical fiction and wasn’t sure what to expect with this story.<br><br>My first reaction when I opened the book up after receiving it? Holy sh*% this is a long book. I’m talking Outlander long. Luckily, a long book does not scare me off. My second reaction after reading the first chapter? This is not going to be a typical romance and <b>I like it!!!</b><br><br>How to describe the story…. Well, let’s start with the main character, Miss Lilly Linton. A secret suffragette in 19th century London, I likened Lilly to a modern-day feminist transported (against her will) back in time, slang, attitude and all. She seemed to be trapped in a time that didn’t know what to do with her, doomed to be enslaved into a life of marriage and children. She was funny, sarcastic and relentless in her pursuit for “freedom”.<br><br>Mr Rikkard Ambrose was very much like every romance novel’s “asshole boss”, but to the extreme. He came across as uncaring and often cruel in his dealings with Lilly. What I loved about their interactions, though, was Lilly’s reaction to him. She never ceased to throw Mr. Ambrose off his game. I found their interactions endlessly amusing.<br><br>This is what I imagine every character’s reactions in the book to be as they were listening to something come out of Lilly’s mouth:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454196828ra/17930237.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454196828ra/17930238.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454196828i/17930239.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The description listed for the book is vague, so I won’t give too much of the story away in my review. I think it is much better to go into blind. I will say that I found life, through Lilly’s eyes, to be sooo funny. I laughed out loud so many times during the story. Her reaction to everything in life made me smile and in turn, the reactions to Lilly’s antics by all of the characters in the story were hilarious.<br><br>This was a very engaging read for me. Truly, I loved every minute of it. I loved the way Lilly gave Mr. Ambrose a run for his money every time he tried to get his way. As the story went on, it was great to see Lilly fighting jealousy and growing emotions for Mr. Ambrose, which went against everything she thought she wanted in life. In particular, her jealous reaction to a lady Mr. Ambrose proclaimed to have feelings for.<br><br> <blockquote>
  <b>“What was it that caught your fancy? Her figure? Her eyes?’<br>‘Her eyes. And her figure, too. And her dress, her manners, and her… well, she does not have anything more to catch fancies with, but all that she does have is very fancy-catching. You could say that I have passionately fallen in love with the entirety of her, not just the individual components.’<br>‘But you like her eyes.’<br>‘Yes, indeed.’<br>‘What is so special about them?’ I demanded to know, still not daring to look up. I had a suspicion why my eyes were stinging, and if it was correct I wanted nothing less than for him to see my face right now. ‘I saw nothing extraordinary about them!’<br>He cleared his throat again. ‘Well… they look very… very ocular, for one thing.’<br>‘What is that supposed to mean?’<br>‘Pardon?’<br>‘This word, “ocular”. What’s that supposed to mean?’<br>‘It is Latin. It is a word denoting everything that refers to eyes.’<br>‘So… what you’re in fact saying is that what’s special about her eyes is that they look very much like eyes.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I loved all of Mr. Ambrose’s employee’s reactions to Lilly, in particular Karim. <br><br> <blockquote>
  <b>“Gesturing to Karim. ‘I can’t let you walk into danger with only him around for protection.’<br>The Mohammedan’s eyes bulged, and I fancy he would have said something pretty explicit, had not Mr Ambrose spoken first.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>I laughed out loud during every ball held throughout the book and the way Lilly treated all of her would-be suitors. <br><br> <blockquote>
  <b>“A few minutes later a cough distracted me, and I looked up only to be confronted with another officer asking me to dance. I turned him down like a bedspread. And the one after that. And the one after the one after that. And the other gentlemen who followed, from captains to colonels, from misters to majors. It was amazing - the more of them I sent packing, the more seemed to pop up everywhere. You’d think that by now they would have gotten the message.”</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Sir Philip and Ella’s story, as a backdrop, was great. What made it truly enjoyable, though, was Lilly’s sarcastic spin on it. She had no patience for Philip’s nonsense nor did she see the world in Ella’s romantic old-fashioned way. I loved the way she looked out for Ella and shielded her from hurt.<br><br>Though the overall arc of the story centered around mystery and danger of a serious nature, Lilly’s exasperated point of view made me giggle through what would have been some very tense moments.<br><br>Thanks so much to the author for giving me the opportunity to read and review this book. It was a very enjoyable read. Looking forward to seeing how Lilly’s story unfolds (and what kind of shenanigans she gets up to) in the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4434355443695579499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1525576639" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1525576639" />
    <a title="Pinky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky"><img alt="Pinky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489855494p2/27523984.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1525576639?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pinky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pinky" href="/user/show/27523984-pinky">Pinky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1525576639" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15422193467610810619"> <i>A huge thank you to Mr. Robert Thier for providing a free Ebook for review. Your book was amazing and I can't wait to read more from you!</i><br/><br/> What did I just read? I am simply amazed with the book that I have no words to express myself. I still can't get over this book. It feels like I need to recover from all of the adventure.<br/><br/><b>When I finished this book this is exactly what had happened:</b><br/><br/> <i>And then, even that was gone, and there was only silence.</i> I sat there, reading the last sentence of the book Stor</span>
  <span id="freeText15422193467610810619" style="display:none"> <i>A huge thank you to Mr. Robert Thier for providing a free Ebook for review. Your book was amazing and I can't wait to read more from you!</i><br><br> What did I just read? I am simply amazed with the book that I have no words to express myself. I still can't get over this book. It feels like I need to recover from all of the adventure.<br><br><b>When I finished this book this is exactly what had happened:</b><br><br> <i>And then, even that was gone, and there was only silence.</i> I sat there, reading the last sentence of the book Storm and Silence by Robert Thier. It was 12:02 AM and I couldn't get over what I had just read. I don't know if I should cry or smile at how awesome the book was but at how it ended. I was frozen and stared at my phone. I was shocked and I clutched my phone and tried to flip the pages of the Ebook. <br> <i>This cannot be the ending, no no no no no, I need more, please let there be more!</i> I thought and continued to flip the pages. Then, I came across the chapter <i>"None Of Your Business"</i> and was excited to read a little bit from Rikkard's point of view.<br> "What are you doing?" a voice said from behind me and I jumped. A few seconds later, I realized that it was my mom. She looked at me like I was a crazy person and said "Why are you on your phone, usually, you would stay up and read?"<br> "I <i>am</i> reading, it's an Ebook, you could read it on your phone."<br> "Technology these days, anyway, are you finished? You have that look on you face that says you are super tired and yet you haven't done anything but <i>read</i> on your phone."<br> "It's because I have just been on a crazy adventure with awesome characters named Lilly and Rikkard. It was so much fu-," I said but was interrupted.<br> "It is 12 AM, there is no time for adventures and stories, I am going to bed, and you have an exam to study for.. It's the day after tomorrow right? Alright, you could continue to babble about the book, but don't be too long, go to bed, okay?"<br> Although I stay up and read all the time, I knew that I had to go to bed and so I went to bed. But I couldn't sleep because I couldn't stop thinking about how the book ended. What will happen next, will all the characters be alright? Are we going on anymore crazy adventures? Will women be recognized and will Lilly be accepted for who she really is? I need to find out.<br> I only slept for 3 hours... It was like I couldn't recover from the book, I had so many questions.<br> <br> <b> And now, I am here and writing this review and I can't wait to hear everyone's thoughts on this book.<b><br><br> <i><b>“Knowledge is power is time is money.” </b></i></b><br><br> If you haven't head about this book, it is about a girl named Lilly Linton who is a 19 years old who believes that females should be treated as equals. Since this book takes place in the 19th century, women are not allowed to do many things other then impress men with their beauty, go to balls, marry and become housewives. This book takes place in London and Lilly lives with her aunt and her sisters. She has no choice but to follow everything that her aunt says and go to balls that shes hates. She wanted to start working so she had a plan. After she succeeded in this plan, Lilly was the secretary of a really mysterious man named Rikkard Ambrose. The only problem was that Mr. Ambrose did not want Miss Lilly Linton to work as his secretary. He wanted Mr. Linton to work as his secretary. In other words, Lilly had to work as a male secretary...<br><br> <i><b>“Life is not about living the safer option. Life is about living a life worth living.”</b></i></b><br><br> While reading this book, people would always ask me why I was laughing and I would tell them about this book and they would give me a weird look. IT'S NOT WEIRD TO LAUGH AT A BOOK, GOSH!<br><br><b>Me when I am reading:</b><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446929512ra/16928435.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> The characters were the highlight to why I loved this book so much. I loved Lilly Linton, she was so easy to relate to. She is so sassy and does not care what other people think. She will say what she wants to say, whenever she wants to say it. But she is strong and brave, it made me want to speak out more for myself. I found her character to be very inspiring because if you know me well, I can't speak up for myself, and I feel like I will more because I will think about the way she does things. Rikkard Ambrose on the other hand is so mysterious, the guy with ice cold eyes, who doesn't show that much emotion. The guy who makes you want to know what he is thinking because he is so silent... Ella is an amazing sister, I loved her character and her side story was kind of like Romeo and Juliet. Lilly's aunt was the worst possible nightmare, she was one of those characters that you want to hide from. Karim is an amazing character too, he is really loyal. Captain Carter was a character who stood out and I really would like to read more about him, he is so funny and interesting.<br><br><b>Me when Lilly's Aunt shows up:</b><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454258821i/17936989._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <i>
  <b>“I would prefer a sword to fight duel, but a pen to plan a war.” </b>
</i><br><br> The introduction to the story wants to keep you reading because it starts off beautifully. The writing was awesome and it just keeps me reading, I forgot all about the real world because I am so focused on what was happening in the book. There were so many things going on and every page had me laughing or scared about what was to come. The plot was another strong point and the suspense keeps you reading. You want to know what is going on, and you want to know more about all of the characters.<br><br> <i>
  <b>“Marriage is supposed to be a union between two equals who love and support each other, not a master-slave relationship in which the man commands a docile woman.” </b>
</i><br><br> The bonds between the characters was another strong point about why I loved this book so much. The bonds made the story more realistic. The bond between Lilly and Ambrose was hilarious and everything they said to each other made me laugh. They were so confused about their feelings and they were always fighting and it was so much fun to read. Karim and Ambrose have a strong connection of trust and I like that a lot. Lilly and her Aunt have an uneasy relationship and I could see why. Lilly and Ella's relationship was so sweet, me and my sister don't have a bond as strong as theirs. All these bonds were a great addition to the story.<br><br> <i>
  <b>“Chains of gold are still chains.”</b>
</i><br><br> The setting of this book in the 19th century was really interesting and I loved how it took place in London. Women and their beautiful dresses, although it was a pain to run in it. Men and how they had all the jobs and how women couldn't vote. :( There were so many things that I learned in this book, it was like a history lesson filled with entertainment. Since I had my History Exam coming up, this book helped out a lot. :)<br><br> <i>
  <b>“His blue-green eyes were dark pools of immeasurable depth, pools you could drown yourself in and never again come up for air.” </b>
</i><br><br> The ending was the only part where my heart dropped. ( I know it's a bit dramatic but that's exactly how I felt!) <br><br>And if someone were to ask me what I did after I read the ending, this is what I would have said:<br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454258821ra/17936990.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> <i>
  <b>“You expect me to come and work for you dressed up as a man?” I gasped.” </b>
</i><br><br> I highly, highly recommend this book to everyone! It won the People's Choice Award in the Wattys 2015, it is hilarious, it has a lot of adventure, and perfect amount of romance. The pace is perfect, there is so much suspense that it kept me reading til the very end, (with a lot of interruptions from studying and duties). I can't wait to read everyone's thoughts on this book! <br><br> <i>
  <b>“A man. A really manly man with a lot of mannishness in his manliness.”</b>
</i> </span>

<div id="review_1523205940" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1523205940" />
    <a title="Henz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19767615-henz"><img alt="Henz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516450827p2/19767615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1523205940?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Henz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Henz" href="/user/show/19767615-henz">Henz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=bad-ass-characters">bad-ass-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=laughed-out-loud">laughed-out-loud</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19767615-henz?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1523205940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2816476325580370550">It’s been a long time since I’ve read historical fictions and I was thankful that when I chance upon reading another one, I full on liked it. I never read on <strong><em>Wattpad</em> </strong>so I have no idea that this story was sensational and the book has its own fandom! Most reviews I’ve seen so far rated 5 stars but I don’t always believe the hype. The cover was not that very captivating, it looks more modern and not fitting of the Victorian Era but I guess the fans were already used to the cover. What compelled me </span>
  <span id="freeText2816476325580370550" style="display:none">It’s been a long time since I’ve read historical fictions and I was thankful that when I chance upon reading another one, I full on liked it. I never read on <strong><em>Wattpad</em> </strong>so I have no idea that this story was sensational and the book has its own fandom! Most reviews I’ve seen so far rated 5 stars but I don’t always believe the hype. The cover was not that very captivating, it looks more modern and not fitting of the Victorian Era but I guess the fans were already used to the cover. What compelled me to read this book were the fan-arts. I was intrigued; I wanted to read the book to see what the hype is all about, also to prove them all wrong, that all those gushing reviews are bollocks!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454432426ra/17961620.gif" alt="" width="530" height="299" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Guess what <em>ifrits</em>?! Lords and ladies! You’re right! Now you can all put your parasols down and hear me out. I like the book okay, I really like it but I do have some issues with it that I liked to point out.<br><br>Set in 19th century, an era when women had no rights to suffrage and no freedom. Women are chained in marriage, can’t own any property and don’t have the license to get a job. <strong>Lillian “Lily” Linton</strong> wants to change that, she’s a <em>feminist</em> and wants to be a <em>suffragette</em> and vote for the rights of women. I think her character was inspired by the real suffragette <em>Christabel Pankhurst</em> and that of <em>Elizabeth Bennet</em> in <strong>Pride and Prejudice. </strong>I love how Lilly was able to bring out her sass and unladylike behavior in the most charming way but though I like her cheekiness she tends to get a little annoying and stubborn at times.<br><br>Dressed as a man, she walked the streets of London to infiltrate a polling station and bumped into a wealthy but very dark and dangerous businessman, <strong>Mr. Rikkard Ambrose</strong>. He offered her a job to his company only he’s in for a big surprise when he learned that what he employed was a female, an abomination, a scandal that will ruin his Empire, this is where all the fun begins!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454432426ra/17961621.gif" alt="" width="349" height="328" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I like how <strong>Robert Thier</strong> was able to create two antagonizing characters; a feminist and chauvinist and somehow able tangle them in a slow burning harmony. Humor is another thing that I liked in this novel, I had a good laugh whenever Lily’s feministic ideas clash with that of Mr. Rikkard Ambrose’s close-minded superior way of thinking. The romance is no insta-love obviously which made it more realistic and you’re going to read the romance part when you're about sixty percent done with the book but oh my it was hot and they’re not even naked! It’s purely wholesome and oh such a tease! LOL<br><br>Another thing, though I like the dark and mysterious Mr. Ambrose, I love him even! Still, I’m quite bothered by his manhandling behaviors to Lily, he’s supposed to a gentleman, and I hate how he denied her, gods I hate it. Uh uh, He's no <strong>Mr. Darcy</strong> everyone. I’m just curious as to why Mr. Ambrose has this over the top brooding personality but I guess I’m just going to wait for the sequel. Another thing that needs to be pointed out were the dragging chapters, most of them were the part with Lily’s sister, <em>Ella</em>. I know it’s significant to Lily’s feelings but I got tired reading about her romance with <em>Edmund</em>. Apart from that I think I enjoyed most of the chapters and I commend how Robert Thier ended each one with suspense not to mention the <em>cliffhanger</em> that almost killed me. Oh the agony!<br><br>Overall this book is a very engaging read, quite <em>spiffing </em>actually (*wink*), a historical fiction mixed with romance and adventure. I highly recommend this book to all kinds of people. (^^)<br><br>~<em>A digital ARC was provided by Author Robert Thier in exchange for an honest review.</em>~</span>
  <a data-text-id="2816476325580370550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1519251959" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1519251959" />
    <a title="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines"><img alt="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466111136p2/30004027.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1519251959?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–" href="/user/show/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines">Laurie –Read Between The Skylines–</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28502955-storm-and-silence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30004027-laurie-read-between-the-skylines?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1519251959" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13677009343001182291"><b>
  <u>Update on December 14th 2016</u>
</b><br/><br/>I initially accepted this ARC because of the book plot as well as its high rating. It wasn't that good for me, but out of respect to the author and his work, I forced myself to the end. <br/><br/>This November, I've noticed that this book came second on "Goodreads Choice Awards 2016" in "Romance" with more than 44.000 votes when this book has only less than 10.000 ratings in total. I didn't pay that much attention back then.<br/><br/>It all really started a couple of days ago, when a</span>
  <span id="freeText13677009343001182291" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Update on December 14th 2016</u>
</b><br><br>I initially accepted this ARC because of the book plot as well as its high rating. It wasn't that good for me, but out of respect to the author and his work, I forced myself to the end. <br><br>This November, I've noticed that this book came second on "Goodreads Choice Awards 2016" in "Romance" with more than 44.000 votes when this book has only less than 10.000 ratings in total. I didn't pay that much attention back then.<br><br>It all really started a couple of days ago, when around 10 new persons liked this review, all of them had no friend, no rating except for Robert Thier's book, all voted for the book for the "Romance" category and all account were created in Nov. 2016. I went to see the top reviews and noticed that all the positives ones were massively liked by the same kinds of profiles as well. The same kind of profiles came up when I sorted the rating by "newest". <b>Hundreds of accounts possibly created with the only purpose to inflate Storm and Silence's rating.</b><br><br>I don't want to imply anything, so I let GR support know and let them make a decision accordingly. <br>However, today, I saw <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1889715934?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly's review</a>. It basically says the same thing, except that it goes further (quote from the author wattpad for instance)<br><br>I really hope that we are both wrong, nonetheless, I needed to write about it.<br><br>__________________________<br><br><b>
  <u>Initial review posted on March 9th 2016.</u>
</b><br><br><i>~ ARC kindly provided by the author, in exchange for an honest review ~</i><br><br><u>Minor spoilers below</u><br><br>Finishing this book resulted in an excruciatingly long inner battle. I almost put it down many times especially in the first half of it.<br><br><b>Actual Rating: 2.25/5 </b><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I would prefer a sword to fight a duel, but a pen to plan a war.”</i>
</blockquote><br><u>“London, August 1839”.</u> The first words of this book were just what I needed. I love the Victorian era in London. It is my favourite period when I wish I would have lived, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18335634.Clockwork_Princess__The_Infernal_Devices___3_" title="Clockwork Princess (The Infernal Devices, #3) by Cassandra Clare" rel="nofollow noopener">Clockwork Princess</a>, one of my favourite series takes place during this same period. When I first read the synopsis, I was like “all right, a book dealing with feminism, but written by a man, it sounds promising, not common, I love this idea. I think I can love this book”, that is the reason why I accepted this ARC. <br><br><u>Let me present you how this book starts:</u> Lilly Linton is an <b>avant-gardist</b>. She lives at a time when Ladies are supposed to behave properly and not question men, wear beautiful gowns and being invited to balls hoping to be spotted by the most eligible bachelors in London. But she doesn’t see it that way. She only wants one thing: FREEDOM. She is what they called a <b>“suffragette”</b> (btw this word was created in 1903, so 65 years after this book), fighting for girls’ rights and liberties. Her main fight: giving women the right to vote. This book begins with Lilly, dressed like a man, with her uncle’s clothes trying to enter the pooling station. On her way, she overhears a conversation between businessmen and <b>gives her advice</b> to one of them who is about to make a <b>risky investment</b>. Satisfied with her help, he decides to hire her, convinced that she is a promising young man. To Lilly, it is a dream becoming true, what she has always wanted; to work to be able to earn money and then to be <b>free from marriage and other obligations toward men</b>. However, she is discovered while trying to vote, and taken by policemen. They are bringing her to the station, she is exposed to her new employer but nonetheless, she tells him that she will be at work the next day.<br><blockquote>
  <i>“Knowledge is power is time is money.”</i>
</blockquote><br>This first chapter got me like: <u>this book has so much potential!</u> It seemed that the author did a lot of researches on the subject and the period. But the more I kept reading, and the more I kept thinking that he doesn’t have a true perception of the womankind. To him, every girl except his main character is satisfied with her lower consideration (or at least they don’t care), they are not asking questions and they are following orders. For instance, when Lilly tries to speak about politic to her sisters, they say <i>‘Oh, leave us alone with your talks of politics and adventure stories and God knows what else, Lilly. We’re too busy with serious talk to be bothered with your nonsense (aka gossips in that case).’</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432793ra/18357460.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The main character was badass at first, but then she started to be <b>childish</b>, <b>stubborn</b> (not in a good way) and <b>hypocrite</b>. To me, <b>both the author and the MC mixed feminism and hatred toward man</b>, which made the book a little bit <b>cliché</b> to me.<br><br>Moreover, the author beat about the bush too much. The book was slow-paced, we had to wait until 20% to have some sort of a story, and at least 50% to have an interesting book. Some parts were awfully repetitive (please put me out of my misery and stop telling yourself that you have to stop thinking about him already!!). It could have been cut in half and still have enough information and in the end, be less boring.<br><br>What I liked about Lilly though was her independence and how fierce, loyal and smart she was (sometimes). We get to see more of that in the second half of the book. She gets back some badassness and I liked that a lot. There are a few scenes that I truly loved in this book, one of them being the ball when Lilly had to pretend to be courteous. It was so much funnier than smart-mouthed-90's-teenager Lilly and I think that it would have been interesting to have more of that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454811250ra/18016907.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I also loved to imagine some scene like for instance the secretary in hoop skirts, and also loved the bar scene. I really enjoyed the love interest and the tension which was often palpable between the two MC. I was like "kiss already!"<br><br>However, I have to wonder if the author has ever been drunk in his life… Lilly seemed more under the effects of drugs than anything else… But it was one of my favourite scenes. Two last things to add;<br> <br>•	<u> The French Island</u>: <br>WTH? Mainly this whole book was full of anachronisms but here, I really don’t know what happened in the author’s mind. This scene is a total rupture of the writing style. It is full of prejudices and absolutely wrong (basically most things about French were). This is what French girls were wearing at the beach in 1875 (37 years after this book takes place). <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457433536i/18357633.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>•	<u>The ending</u>: <br>I will have elaborate nor comment on that except that to me it is almost <b>plagiarism</b>. Will understand those who have read this book (at least those who went to the end of it).</span>
  <a data-text-id="13677009343001182291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer11384776647668327388">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to author Robert Thier.)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That’s exactly what I intend! Votes, ladies and gentlemen, votes for women!”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455380698i/18095575._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This was a YA historical novel, about a girl who wanted women to be equal to men.<br/><br/>Lillian/Lily was quite a head-strong character, and she was determined to make a stand and make people see that women were just as capable as men, even if her methods were a little naïve!<br/>Mr Ambrose was also quite a </span>
  <span id="freeText11384776647668327388" style="display:none">(Source: I received a digital copy of this book for free on a read-to-review basis. Thanks to author Robert Thier.)<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“That’s exactly what I intend! Votes, ladies and gentlemen, votes for women!”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455380698i/18095575._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was a YA historical novel, about a girl who wanted women to be equal to men.<br><br>Lillian/Lily was quite a head-strong character, and she was determined to make a stand and make people see that women were just as capable as men, even if her methods were a little naïve!<br>Mr Ambrose was also quite a character, and his letters that he wrote were certainly to the point, even if Lily thought them rude.<br><br>The storyline in this was about Lily bluffing her way into a man’s job working as a secretary to Mr Ambrose, and then about a missing document, which Mr Ambrose was intent on finding. The pace in this was really slow though, and I found that I would want to put this down after only a couple of chapters.<br>There was a bit of romance, but it was very slow, and we didn’t get much!<br><br>The ending to this was a giant cliff-hanger!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433081147i/15047180.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6.5 out of 10</span>

Far from being one of those corny romantic stories, Rob Thier's novel succeeds in creating an intense tension between the reckless Lilly and the handsome yet dangerous Ambrose. Moreover, the plotline draws our attention to the condition of women, which makes the book even more subtle and brilliant (Lilly's speach while the demonstr</span>
  <span id="freeText15191155310560543705" style="display:none">This is not just some fiction, it is an incredibly well-written and intelligent book, with the most interesting characters and a real reflection on the Victorian era. Far from being one of those corny romantic stories, Rob Thier's novel succeeds in creating an intense tension between the reckless Lilly and the handsome yet dangerous Ambrose. Moreover, the plotline draws our attention to the condition of women, which makes the book even more subtle and brilliant (Lilly's speach while the demonstration is indeed "memorable"). The author's talent is undeniable, for his sharp humour and his incredible capacity to describe the authentic Victorian England. <br />In short, I would have never thought I could say that about a Wattpad fiction but it really is a GREAT book (that deserves to be edited in a real proper one I think).</span>
