    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1535900753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1535900753" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18780551-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520389159p2/18780551.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1535900753?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/18780551-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=own-on-kindle">own-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=not-my-cup-of-tea">not-my-cup-of-tea</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=victorian-era">victorian-era</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=not-finished">not-finished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18780551-anne?shelf=review-requests">review-requests</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1535900753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8960362488217213387"><b>DNF at 8%</b>. This is a case of "this book is really not my thing and I don't want to waste time with it" as opposed to "this book was so horrible I couldn't finish it", so I won't give it a rating. <br/><br/>If you don't know anything about the Victorian era, don't know that women couldn't vote, that they wore petticoats, crinolines and their hair up, that their role was to embroider cushions, hem handkerchiefs and produce heirs, then perhaps you will appreciate this tale told in first person POV by the her</span>
  <span id="freeText8960362488217213387" style="display:none"><b>DNF at 8%</b>. This is a case of "this book is really not my thing and I don't want to waste time with it" as opposed to "this book was so horrible I couldn't finish it", so I won't give it a rating. <br /><br />If you don't know anything about the Victorian era, don't know that women couldn't vote, that they wore petticoats, crinolines and their hair up, that their role was to embroider cushions, hem handkerchiefs and produce heirs, then perhaps you will appreciate this tale told in first person POV by the heroine, who seems to be telling her story to a modern audience she assumes knows nothing about the Victorian era. If, on the other hand, you are a high stickler for historical accuracy and your definition of an independent, strong Victorian female protagonist is something along the lines of Miss Jane Eyre, I wouldn't recommend this novel. <br /><br />The heroine, Lilly Linton, <b>does not at all</b> depict a 19th century suffragette bent on fighting for women's rights. She most definitely comes across as a 21st century feminist about to free bleed in front of Parliament. She doesn't just want equal rights for both genders. Miss Lilly is out there to prove that women are <b>superior</b> to men. With her it's "men are jerks, men know nothing, I don't like men, I don't want men, I don't need men". That is modern-day thinking. <br /><br /><i>"I disliked all men as a matter of principle, but handsome men, especially ones with a strong chin and overbearing manner, were at the top of my 'things to exterminate to make this world a better place' list."</i> <br /><br />And it's not just her attitude that comes across as modern, but the way she talks and acts. <br /><br /><i>"Hurriedly, I placed myself behind the last man in the line, thanking the Lord the British government hadn't yet adopted the practice of putting pictures of people in passports."</i><br /><br />The book seems to be written with the intent to educate readers about the early Victorian era, but instead of making us learn by creating an authentic atmosphere and developing characters that act true to the period, we have a heroine telling her story to modern readers whom she assumes know nothing of her time and practices. How does she know that there WILL be pictures in passport at a future date? She makes sure to explain the smallest things, to make sure we understand the lives of women in 1838. She dresses up in men's clothes to go voting at a poll station, and makes sure to explain that in England, women aren't allowed to vote. She describes her breakfast to every last detail to make sure we understand that Victorian women did not just grab a bagel on the go, but had to sit down to a full, proper meal in the morning. She makes sure to tell us a calling card is a rectangular piece of cardboard. She highlights the fact that women in England must learn to embroider and work at home. And she makes sure to tell us that women as supposed to be wearing dresses. <br /><br />The thing is, Lilly should be narrating as though people of HER time were reading her story, not <i>us</i>. She isn't supposed to know about us!! That way, there would be no need to specifically state that the government of England doesn't allow women to vote, or that breakfast was an important meal, or that normal, non-Lilly women were supposed to enjoy gossip and society outings. Those things would still be included, but should be written about in a way that assumes the reader already KNOWS how Victorian society functions. That way, you still learn things about the era, but you have to pick up the clues for yourself, as opposed to having all the infos dumped at you by a heroine who isn't supposed to know that her readers don't live in 1838. <br /><br />As I've said before, if really you didn't know all this already about the Victorian era and don't mind a modern-minded heroine as the main character, this book will work for you just fine. It's well-written if you're not looking for an authentic early-Victorian feel, the plot is rather good if incredibly slow, and the romance seemed somewhat promising. I was interested in the hero enough that I pushed on reading until he met again with the heroine, at which point he offers her a job as his secretary provided she come to work dressed as a man, and that is where I decided I couldn't take anymore and it was better for me just to stop before I grew <i>really</i> exasperated. <br /><br />I was able to overlook the anachronistic cover and the fact that the heroine cross-dresses, since some of my top favourite books feature both those issues, but I honestly don't have the patience for a heroine who says things like:<br /><br /><i>"Running from my problems had never been my style. Grabbing them by the throat and shaking them until they capitulated, that was more my way of dealing with things."</i><br /><br />and<br /><br /><i>"I was wearing trousers! Why is that infamous? They're just a piece of cloth and don't make me any less of a girl. If you went around dressed in a ball gown, would that make you any less of a man?"</i><br /><br />and<br /><br /><i>"We have been kept down for centuries, but you'll see, one day women will conquer their rightful place in the world! One day there will be hundreds, maybe thousands of women working as secretaries. We will be so good at it that we will put men out of their jobs, and just about secretary will be female!"</i><br /><br />Just. So. Modern. <br /><br />This book would have worked so much better if it had been a time-travel romance where the heroine WAS from the 21st century and rebelled and sought to change the position of women in the 19th century. But it wasn't, and Lilly was way too modern to be believable. If she really wanted a job, she would have become a governess. That's what women did in the Victorian era when they were impoverished. This book did not even <i>mention</i> the word governess. Lilly belonged to a really, <i>really</i> poor family, who despite their completely reduced circumstances, still went out into high society parties and had incredibly high social and marriage aspirations.<br /><br />I like my historical romances <i>historical</i>. There's a reason I tend to stay away from contemporary-set novels. <br /><br />I was provided a free copy of this book in exchange for an honest review. Many thanks to the author for this opportunity, and I'm sorry I wasn't able to finish it. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8960362488217213387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1312414827" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312414827" />
    <a title="Caitlyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29732377-caitlyn"><img alt="Caitlyn" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312414827?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caitlyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caitlyn" href="/user/show/29732377-caitlyn">Caitlyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312414827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8347539049958189373">I was a little surprised to say the least when I first started the book and saw that women weren't allowed to vote.. (this might have something to do with the fact that I very briefly skimmed over the blurb and didn't notice it was set wayy back in 19th century England). As someone who normally doesn't read historical romance, this book was quite enjoyable and funny in many parts. <br/><br/>I was expecting the tone to be considerably more serious and focused on <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[the suffragette movement <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hid</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText8347539049958189373" style="display:none">I was a little surprised to say the least when I first started the book and saw that women weren't allowed to vote.. (this might have something to do with the fact that I very briefly skimmed over the blurb and didn't notice it was set wayy back in 19th century England). As someone who normally doesn't read historical romance, this book was quite enjoyable and funny in many parts. <br><br>I was expecting the tone to be considerably more serious and focused on <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the suffragette movement <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but the exchanges between Lilly and Mr. Ambrose were so amusing that I just got absorbed into the story. Lilly was a strong female protaganist, headstrong and dense at times, but still generally lovable. And can we just talk about Mr. Rikkard Ambrose for a second here? He's nothing short of what Austen's Darcy is: cold, brooding, but secretly <i>warm</i> inside. I suspect he is really <i>more warm</i> than we gave him credit for because everytime there was a Lilly and Mr. Ambrose scene, all I could think was:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/522550.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Even though the romance only started to pick up near the end, I'm totally okay with it since it is supposed to be a historical romance. And now I'm just patiently waiting for Rob to stop this agonizing pain I've been feeling all day for being fed the worst possible cliffhanger ever.<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434756509ra/15259414.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1518461704" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1518461704" />
    <a title="S.M. West" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18424676-s-m-west"><img alt="S.M. West" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564323942p2/18424676.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1518461704?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="S.M. West" class="user" itemprop="url" name="S.M. West" href="/user/show/18424676-s-m-west">S.M. West</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781311250056" href="/book/show/28500366-storm-and-silence">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18424676-s-m-west?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1518461704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2271674392222205769"><b>3.75 STARS</b><br/><br/>This story takes place in 19th century London where women can’t vote, work and really don’t have many rights. <br/><br/>Some would classify Lilly Linton as a feminist; I’d say she was a strong, determined and intelligent heroine. Her POV was witty, funny – at times, her inner dialogue had me chuckling. Lilly finds employment with Rikkard Ambrose, a powerful, silent and direct man, provided she disguises herself as a man.<br/><br/>This tale unfolds as these two work together and a letter goes missing that </span>
  <span id="freeText2271674392222205769" style="display:none"><b>3.75 STARS</b><br /><br />This story takes place in 19th century London where women can’t vote, work and really don’t have many rights. <br /><br />Some would classify Lilly Linton as a feminist; I’d say she was a strong, determined and intelligent heroine. Her POV was witty, funny – at times, her inner dialogue had me chuckling. Lilly finds employment with Rikkard Ambrose, a powerful, silent and direct man, provided she disguises herself as a man.<br /><br />This tale unfolds as these two work together and a letter goes missing that Mr. Ambrose is desperate to find. This was well written and these two characters were interesting however, I found the story dragged at times with some repetition and lengthy prose. There is also a bit of romance but it’s not front and centre. Still, this was a refreshing story and I must say, it ends on a cliffhanger. <br /><br />**ARC generously provided by author in exchange for an honest review.**</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1522112117" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1522112117" />
    <a title="Hana ♡" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31716629-hana"><img alt="Hana ♡" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1522112117?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hana ♡" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hana ♡" href="/user/show/31716629-hana">Hana ♡</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=mega-rich-hero">mega-rich-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=hung-me-over-a-cliff">hung-me-over-a-cliff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=bad-ass-heroine">bad-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31716629-hana?shelf=laughed-my-ass-off">laughed-my-ass-off</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522112117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5515509673176087238"><b>Wow.</b> This book blew me away. I finished this last night and was staring at my ceiling wide awake trying to figure out my feelings.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453488553ra/17834621.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So Lilly is a feminist that lives in 19th century London where women cannot work, or vote. And the only aspirations in life are to get married and be dependent on a husband. This obviously doesn't work with her.<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453825684ra/17877640.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>She ends up acquiring a job working for the notorious, powerful, and intimidating Mr. Ambrose by <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[. disguising herself as a boy. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> </span>
  <span id="freeText5515509673176087238" style="display:none"><b>Wow.</b> This book blew me away. I finished this last night and was staring at my ceiling wide awake trying to figure out my feelings.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453488553ra/17834621.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So Lilly is a feminist that lives in 19th century London where women cannot work, or vote. And the only aspirations in life are to get married and be dependent on a husband. This obviously doesn't work with her.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453825684ra/17877640.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She ends up acquiring a job working for the notorious, powerful, and intimidating Mr. Ambrose by <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[. disguising herself as a boy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The story follows her pursuit for independence in her work and family life getting into many whacky and dangerous situations with Mr. Ambrose. Reading her thoughts was truly a joy, the author made her personality so funny and easygoing that it was nice to escape into the world of Lilly Linton for a while.<br><br>I found it hilarious how she denied the attraction she felt towards Mr. Ambrose because she felt she was betraying her feminist ways...<br><br><b>"I was a proud suffragette and should be thinking about promoting women's rights, not the contents of men's tights!"</b><br><br>Now I have read some pretty raunchy and descriptive sex scenes in romance novels over the years. And I've come to expect them in every romance novel I read, but there really weren't any scenes like that in this book. But somehow I felt the passion that Lilly and Mr. Ambrose felt for each other without the need to constantly pledge their love and passion for one another. He had his own way of caring for her and it really showed in his mannerism without spelling it out. I really wish wish wish that they told each other how they felt but the novel just left me wanting more! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1453635634ra/17852060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't wait to read the next book!! That cliffhanger almost killed me. My heart broke a little when I saw the words <b>THE END.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420098766ra/13171820.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Copy received by author for honest review</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5515509673176087238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104884953-apoorva?shelf=antiheroes-bad-boys">antiheroes-bad-boys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104884953-apoorva?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104884953-apoorva?shelf=enemies-to-lovers">enemies-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104884953-apoorva?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/104884953-apoorva?shelf=office-romance">office-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3445358081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer469637201083850542"><b>4-4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Forgot to mention: This is fairly unrealistic too, since I'd never believe the dress up could fool people as much as it did. Also, the term suffragist was brought to use in 1906 not in 1839. And the stereotyping of various countries like India, USA, France got a little....out of hand at a few places.<br/><br/>And I totally digged the fanart, I mean: <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221776i/29894360._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='250' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221776i/29894358.jpg' width='300' height='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221776i/29894359._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>And you need the memes, you need them in your life. Search them now. I'll give you one:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221828i/29894363._SX540_.jpg' width='300' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>She's hardcore into that shit, I can attest.<br/><br/>Okay, this h</span>
  <span id="freeText469637201083850542" style="display:none"><b>4-4.5 stars</b><br><br>Forgot to mention: This is fairly unrealistic too, since I'd never believe the dress up could fool people as much as it did. Also, the term suffragist was brought to use in 1906 not in 1839. And the stereotyping of various countries like India, USA, France got a little....out of hand at a few places.<br><br>And I totally digged the fanart, I mean: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221776i/29894360._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="250" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221776i/29894358.jpg" width="300" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221776i/29894359._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>And you need the memes, you need them in your life. Search them now. I'll give you one:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596221828i/29894363._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>She's hardcore into that shit, I can attest.<br><br>Okay, this had every potential of being a 5 star for me. I loved the characters, to death. In the start, I felt like dropping it at the 20% mark, but I'm glad I didn't. But let's get over the part(s) that held me back first:<br><br>1. <b>This is a historical romance book but the writing didn't feel like it. It felt a mix between historical and contemporary, which worked in my favor since although I'm a 'classics' person, I'm not a historical romance person.</b><br><br>2.Lilly is supposed to be a feminist, but it felt more like she was anti-men, totally prejudiced against that particular breed of humankind and to be honest, if I were alive during that time and had to hear what men said, I would be anti-men too. But I don't like that it's called feminism, because it's technically incorrect. But I loved her! <br><br>3. The number of times she mentioned how 'cold' and 'stoic' Mr Ambrose was- it felt like the starting of an ice age. It didn't irritate me much, but sure as heck wasn't required as much too. Plus sometimes I wondered if anyone could be that stoic-<i> je n'en pense pas mes amis.</i> <br><br>4. I get why he called her 'Mr Linton' almost all the time, since she was dressed as a man, but they both knew it was just a pretense for the outer world and him calling her Mr in private didn't bother me because I think he wanted to maintain the distance, so as to not fall for her (kiss your delusions goodbye, Ambrose), but in some situations, I would've preferred Miss.<br><br>5. At first when Ambrose was introduced, it was like seeing Roarke(In Death series) and my eyes glazed over- literally. But <i>blasphemy!</i> Rikkard Ambrose is a fuckin' miser. I hate misers. You are the richest man in London- own seventy percent of hotels there and you're a miser? <i>Disgrace</i>. Roarke indulged in his wealth, almost too much, and this man hoards it like he's taking it with him after he dies. But....but.....fudge it, I love him. <br><br>Hmm, I think this was all, apart from some little things, insignificant really.<br><br><b>Now, I <i>loved</i> the banter- it was witty, childish at some places, but totally hilarious and it's my crack in books. Lilly was an amazing character- fiery, courageous, smart, wise (okay not that much), and above all gave it as good as she got it! She was just a 19 year old girl, a suffragist fighting for her rights with her amazing friends, and somehow ended up tangled with the coldest man I've ever read- Mr Ambrose. He was a tough nut, icy cold, frigid really, reserved, silent, broody but he did really like her, even if his first impressions were.....ahem.....faulty. Really faulty.</b> I'm sure his left little finger will agree with my inference. (Read the book, you'll understand)<br>I liked some of the secondary characters too, but the younger sister and her secret lover have to take the award for the cheesiest, cringiest people alive, who won my heart over. I absolutely cannot go without mentioning Captain Carter, even though he had like two chapters- that man was total BFF material. I think there might be a little romantic interest from his side in the next books, but I hope it doesn't get too much because I'd hate to not cheer for him, since yeah, Mr Ambrose still is my nominee for who-wins-Lilly's-heart award (you're halfway there man, don't disappoint me).<br><br>And the sexual tension? Seeped through the pages, but was dampened by that Mister sometimes too *side eyed glare*. And the first kiss (es) were so good, I would have loved them if not for the fact that Lilly was drunk. Oooh well. Still liked them. <i>A lot</i>.<br><br>And I knew the book was going to end on a cliffhanger and I <i>know</i> they both will get together again (not in the relationship sense, that hasn't even started folks), but the ending still hurt like hell. I'll let it simmer before picking the next one, I want to space this series as long as I can.</span>

  <span id="freeText10005894796916892049" style="display:none">Positive - This may have sucked any will I usually have to want books to be longer. For at least a month. I'm guessing in the next book we'll get more his background story but here without it, he never made a big impression on me. <br> <br>There was a secondary romance with the heroine's sister but it was so childish, exaggerated, and over-the-top with the conversations and proclaimed love between the couple that started skipping any pages/scenes dedicated to them, I just couldn't, y'all. <br> <br>I didn't see a young adult categorization but I would place it under that. There were footnotes on a decent amount of historical words/events mentioned in the story that it felt like an acknowledgement to beginning readers. Also, the only thing that makes this historical is because the author placed it during English woman's suffrage. The speech/language of heroine and characters is extremely modern. <br> <br>This was a Goodreads best of 2016 nominee, obviously I'm in the minority but I won't be continuing in the series because:<br>I've read, like, 600pgs and I don't even feel romance.<br>Oh, that's because there's no love or sex in there.<br>So I'm just reading, like a kid?<br>What is happening at these best of romance rewards is ridiculous.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1542651359?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry" href="/user/show/16188188-kerry">Kerry</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1542651359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11900545197382989609">I received a free copy of this book in exchange for a review. <br/>At first I wasn't sure what to think as the author has hit on a unique approach to the story with it having Historical fiction, Mystery, Romance and Adventure all in one. I wasn't sure how so many facets could be brought together or if it would make for an enjoyable read. Well it certainly did indeed as Robert Thier has a skill for telling a story that is intriguing, exciting and mysterious. <br/>Storm and Silence is based around two main </span>
  <span id="freeText11900545197382989609" style="display:none">I received a free copy of this book in exchange for a review. <br />At first I wasn't sure what to think as the author has hit on a unique approach to the story with it having Historical fiction, Mystery, Romance and Adventure all in one. I wasn't sure how so many facets could be brought together or if it would make for an enjoyable read. Well it certainly did indeed as Robert Thier has a skill for telling a story that is intriguing, exciting and mysterious. <br />Storm and Silence is based around two main characters, the irrepressible Lily Linton and the inimitable Mr Rikkard Ambrose. Lily is on a mission fighting for freedom and the rights of herself and other women to be treated as equals to men, including supporting the efforts of the Suffragette movement. In her schemes to do this she meets Rikkard Ambrose a powerful business man. The book follows their story and the dangerous mysterious world that Mr Ambrose inhabits. <br />It is a thoroughly enjoyable book with lots of twists, turns and unexpected revelations at times. A story of suffrage, power, underhand dealings, family, relationships, secret machinations of powerful organizations, adventure, danger, mystery, societal pressures and restrictions, plus love in different guises. It's a thoroughly enjoyable page turner and I would like to see more books developed with these characters, I think it would make a great series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11900545197382989609" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1532798316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1532798316" />
    <a title="ily " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22496761-ily"><img alt="ily " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599357419p2/22496761.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1532798316?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ily " class="user" itemprop="url" name="ily " href="/user/show/22496761-ily">ily </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22496761-ily?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1532798316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17572188972468542694"><i>*Digital copy kindly provided by the author in exchange for an honest review. Thank you very much.</i><br/><br/>3.5/5 stars<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>I cannot and will not accept a female secretary. I will not be made a fool of in front of the entire city. Either you come dressed as a man, or you never return.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>That was such a lovely surprised!</b> I did not expect this book to be so <i>entertaining</i>. Historical Fiction is not a genre I read often, but this author kindly aproached me asking if I was interested in reading his novel, and of co</span>
  <span id="freeText17572188972468542694" style="display:none"><i>*Digital copy kindly provided by the author in exchange for an honest review. Thank you very much.</i><br><br>3.5/5 stars<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I cannot and will not accept a female secretary. I will not be made a fool of in front of the entire city. Either you come dressed as a man, or you never return.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>That was such a lovely surprised!</b> I did not expect this book to be so <i>entertaining</i>. Historical Fiction is not a genre I read often, but this author kindly aproached me asking if I was interested in reading his novel, and of course I said yes. <i>Storm and Silence</i> was hell of a fun read. Not the book of my life, but it did keep up reading all night and had lovely characters that made me laugh A LOT. <br><br>First off I have to say that at first sign this doesn't look like a YA book. The suited man on the cover gives me New Adult/Erotic novel vibes. Also, it is not appealing to me; so many men on covers nowadays! - it bores me. <br><br>The book takes place in the 19th century London. Lillian Linton is a young feminist girl who wants to work towards getting suffrage for women. Lillian wishes to get a job, not having to depend from her uncle's money or any other man's. But obviously in those days no woman was allowed to vote or -even worst!- make a living. No one in their sane mind would ever think of giving jobs to the female population. How crazy! That is until one of the richest men in the Britain Empire does it. Poor Mr Ambrose didn't know he was hiring a girl as his secretary. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415606253ra/11817583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Don't hate me for this, Lilly, but I would have had you fired inmediately.</i> I admire Mr Ambrose patience. He did not succumb to Lillian's crazy personality and lack of professionalism. Lilly was such a lively young girl. Funny, even hilarious! But she wasn't that good at her job. If I were busy with work and my secretary were distracting me by asking too many questions and trying to get into my personal business, I would have that person dismiss. Lilly made me laugh so hard, but in real life I wouldn't have her under my employ. <i>Nothing personal, Lilly.</i><br><br>That doesn't mean I hated her character. She was <b>refresing</b>; didn't care about other people's opinions nor wasn't afraid of telling others what was on her mind. Certainly she wasn't shy, but she faught for what she believe in, and that is something I respect.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Now that you are regularly running around in men’s clothes you might as well claim male privileges, such as shooting anybody whose face you didn’t like.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Isn't she lovely?<br><br><i>My eyes narrowed. I didn’t know much about etiquette, but I did know that the inferior person was always introduced to the superior. By deciding to introduce me to his friend and not the other way around, he had put me on a level below him. And that was something, considering the complacent smile on the lieutenant’s face, which I did not appreciate at all.</i><br><br>This is an actual pic of lovely Miss Linton.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455735107i/18144191._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mr Ambrose woudn't refer to her as Miss while she were under his employ, but that didn't slow her down. One of my favorite aspects about Lilly is that she <i>hold on to her principles</i>. No man was ever going to talk her out of them. She kept her mind on what was right and important to her, and didn't fear to fight back to those who made fun of her for thinking outside the box. Nor was she insecure, and that is something I always find atractive in a character. To me Lillian was more like a friend. Her disastrous seek for acceptance and adventure was a hell of fun to read. It didn't give me any rest. However, I wish she were a bit more cautious under certain situations. <i>Getting oneself into trouble isn't a brilliant idea, Lilly</i>. The adventurous part of her loved it but, was it really necessary to be joining Mr Ambrose in every likely-to-get-you-killed situation? <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444149291ra/16459553.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote><i>An image flashed in front of my eyes: I, entering the big hall downstairs, in an undoubtedly feminine dress, my head held high, going up to work for one of London’s most powerful businessmen. The first ever lady to earn her own way in this world...</i></blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383704830ra/6639145.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The love interest in this book was a JERK.</b> <i>You heard right, Mr Ambrose.</i> Lucky for this book I have a soft spot for jerks. Mr Ambrose. Mr Ambrose. Mr Ambrose. How is it?? Oh right, <i>Knowledge is power is time is money!</i> That richy bastard gave me a headache and a rising urge to kill. I hated him, but also found him very..... readable. <b>He was a nice jerk.</b> (Forgive me for trying to find positive adjetives to describe him.) Lilly said he was a modern Mr Darcy who woudn't spend a thousand pounds on anybody, and she was right. God, that man was cheap! Imagine having one of the wealthiest gentleman in the country as your boss, but that person wouldn't do anything for anyone. At all. Mr Ambrose was so uptight and self-centered that I thought I'd hate hate for the rest of my read.<br><br><i><blockquote>Oh how I would have loved to skin that man alive. And then maybe roast him slowly over an open fire...</blockquote></i><br><br>My thoughts exactly. What a horrible boss!! <br><br><blockquote><i>It wasn’t long until my feet began to ache and I had numerous paper cuts on my fingers from hastily leafing through files. When I got bloodstains on one of them, he accused me of wilfully damaging company material and ordered me to stop bleeding.</i></blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1388174595ra/7755647.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Was he always like this? Mostly, yeah. Ambrose didn't <i>do feelings</i>. His romantic relationship with Lilly didn't begin until a couple hundred pages, and I am really thankful for that. The instalove would have destroyed my positive thoughts about the book. I must admit that I am so into the love/hate type of romance. I don't know why but I love it when a couple doesn't get along but instead share a mutual hate for each other. Their constant fights over simple subjects made this a pleasing and fast-paced book, and it was definitely my favorite part of it. <br><br>The ending broke my heart. I didn't love it or hate it - I just wish it hadn't looked so rushed. It felt like there were still more pages to read but they had been cut short. <b>How is it possible to end a book like that?! It is not fair and it should be illegal!</b> I didn't sign up to get my hopes high and then end up this messy with my feelings. You don't do that to someone who's enjoying you're book! YOU JUST DON'T!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455735107i/18144192.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So that was me ranting over the messy (and painful) ending. But the rest of the book was just great. If I had had more time to read I would've finished this long ago (Damn you, life!) But overall the story was well-built and its characters weren't such a pain in the ass. I just had few issues: a) To me it felt a bit too similar to <i>Pride &amp; Prejudice</i> sometimes - with the sister in love and the rest of the annoying relatives as backgroud, but that was normal family at that time, b) How did Lilly convince her family to not care about where she went all day? Weren't girls in that period highly guarded?, and c) Ah, couldn't they just accept the fact they were in love?! For once I thought I was gonna punch someone (my brother who was there while I read) in the face because they were oblivious to the tension around them! Lilly kept asking herself why would Mr Ambrose care about her well-being, and that just tiring since their chemistry was a palpable thing. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1443381562ra/16354093.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I would highly recommend <i>Storm and Silence</i> because even when it was not a perfect book, I believe everyone should be able to enjoy the pleasure of hating -and loving- Mr Ambrose. You just be careful with the ending - it hurts a little. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17572188972468542694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1446282486" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1446282486" />
    <a title="Fukiya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49134513-fukiya"><img alt="Fukiya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463508193p2/49134513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1446282486?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fukiya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fukiya" href="/user/show/49134513-fukiya">Fukiya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49134513-fukiya?shelf=might-as-well-stab-me">might-as-well-stab-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446282486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9848102191986206014">Okay, before I start, I would like to say that I—out of self-preservation—generally stay away from Wattpad. Unlike Fictionpress or other online story archives, Wattpad does not allow users to sort stories based on number of favorites, reviews, or ratings. Thus, more often than not, a story is a miss rather than a hit, and by ‘miss’, I mean can’t-hit-the-broad-side-of-a-barn miss. <br/><br/>That being said, this story is truly a wonderful read. The story is set in 1839, shortly after Queen Victoria began h</span>
  <span id="freeText9848102191986206014" style="display:none">Okay, before I start, I would like to say that I—out of self-preservation—generally stay away from Wattpad. Unlike Fictionpress or other online story archives, Wattpad does not allow users to sort stories based on number of favorites, reviews, or ratings. Thus, more often than not, a story is a miss rather than a hit, and by ‘miss’, I mean can’t-hit-the-broad-side-of-a-barn miss. <br /><br />That being said, this story is truly a wonderful read. The story is set in 1839, shortly after Queen Victoria began her reign, and right when the Industrial Revolution in England picked up steam (haha, get it? Because one of the major innovations during the time period was the steam engine, and I just said that the Revolution picked up… okay, I’ll stop). The main protagonist is a feminist named Lilly Linton who <s>deviously tricked</s> <i>politely</i> convinced a rich, powerful businessman named Rikkard Ambrose into hiring her as his secretary. <br /><br />Now, this is a very common cliché—rich, powerful man gets stuck with ordinary, not-very-powerful-at-all girl. And normally, I would have rolled my eyes into the back of my head and exited the web browser. But Robert Thier's amusing writing style got me to continue reading, and I'm glad I did.<br /><br />I could write a dozen pages on why I enjoy reading this book, but I'm sure the majority of them have already been written about in other reviews. However, I have three personal big reasons why I like this story, and they are: the characters, the history, and the writing style. <br /><br />First—the characters. One of the reasons I stayed with this book is because the characters are <i>human.</i> I’ll say that one more time: The. Characters. Are. Human. And I don’t mean just by species. Every character in this story is three-dimensional, with their own personal thoughts, feelings, behaviors, actions, etc. that make them feel real. None of them are perfect. Lilly makes mistakes every now and then and even Rikkard is shown to slip up on occasions. And most importantly, Lilly and Rikkard’s worlds do <i>not</i> revolve around each other. As the book is written from Lilly’s POV, a good chunk of the book is focused on her family and friends, which in turn influences her decisions and actions. They’re not permanently attached at the hip, which is a good thing in both romance stories and real life relationships. <br /><br />Second—the history. I love historical fiction, and will scrutinize every story I read for historical accuracy. Storm and Silence is remarkably accurate in both setting and events. Everything from the unit of measurement to the etiquette of introductions is integrated into the story. I don’t know much about the history of the Victorian Era, but every time I find an interesting fact or tidbit, I always go back to the story to see if I can find it, and so far, I’ve found all but one. If you love the Victorian era, I highly suggest you check out this book. <br /><br />Third—the writing style. Robert Thier possesses a unique sort of humor that shows in his writing. You know how when you read something funny online, you usually just exhale a bit harder instead of actually laughing? I really laughed when reading Storm and Silence. Really. I’m not going to say at what part, because spoilers, but I definitely chuckled. The plotline itself is full of twists and turns. Sir Rob has the <s>very, very, very, VERY bad habit of putting cliffhangers at the end of every chapter</s> tendency to steer the plotline off the rails, so to speak. Suspenseful moments can quickly turn casual, and casual moments can quickly turn suspenseful. He always leaves the readers guessing, and it’s difficult to predict how events will unfold, and that’s what makes this story such an interesting read. <br /><br />Overall, this story is very much a slow-burn sort of romance, which I greatly enjoy. The characters are lovable (or at least relatable), the history is accurate, and the writing is excellent. <br /><br />So, if I enjoy this story so much, why did I rate it 4 stars instead of 5? Well, you see, Rikkard did something to Lilly that he hasn’t apologized for, and I—being me—can’t just dismiss that so easily. I do not accept “because they’re hot” as an excuse for bad behavior. I like my male romance characters to be attractive, confident, and HELD RESPONSIBLE FOR THEIR ACTIONS LIKE EVERYONE ELSE. <br /><br />Okay, that wasn’t the real reason this got 4 stars (but I still think he should be held accountable). The actual reason is that a few of the scenes tend to feel a bit long. Like, for example, the scenes with Lilly’s sister and someone in a rendezvous. The scenes don’t <i>actually</i> drag on, because they are a big influence on Lilly’s decisions, but I feel like that scene in particular would have a lot more impact if Thier emphasized on the social consequences of… what Lilly’s sister almost did. This is a wonderful book, but it could be greatly improved through some editing and rewriting. <br /><br />But hey—this book hasn’t been professionally published yet as of me writing this. Who knows? Maybe I’ll turn my review into a 5-star after reading the published version. <br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9848102191986206014" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1632349629" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632349629" />
    <a title="Sofi Mascaró" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51975219-sofi-mascar"><img alt="Sofi Mascaró" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487254834p2/51975219.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632349629?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sofi Mascaró" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sofi Mascaró" href="/user/show/51975219-sofi-mascar">Sofi Mascaró</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51975219-sofi-mascar?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51975219-sofi-mascar?shelf=books-read-in-english">books-read-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51975219-sofi-mascar?shelf=heart-breaking-books">heart-breaking-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51975219-sofi-mascar?shelf=pdf-kindle-wattpad">pdf-kindle-wattpad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51975219-sofi-mascar?shelf=books-in-english">books-in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51975219-sofi-mascar?shelf=collabs">collabs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632349629" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2902082173031976027"><b>
  <i>Thank you so much to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6123144.Robert_Thier' title='Robert Thier' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robert Thier</a> for providing me a free copy of your book in exchange for an honest review! </i>
</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>‘Chains of gold are still chains, Mr Ambrose. I want to decide what to do with my life.’</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I'm in a huge mess right now.<br/>I'm not a fan of reading either my phone or my computer but I decided to change that just during May and check out this book set in the Victorian era (the one I'm just studying right now in my career)...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464793689ra/19277621.gif' width='200' height='200/' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464794188ra/19277728.gif' width='200' height='200/' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So this is how I'm feeling right now.<br/><br/>The story follows Lilly </span>
  <span id="freeText2902082173031976027" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Thank you so much to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6123144.Robert_Thier" title="Robert Thier" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Thier</a> for providing me a free copy of your book in exchange for an honest review! </i>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>‘Chains of gold are still chains, Mr Ambrose. I want to decide what to do with my life.’</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I'm in a huge mess right now.<br>I'm not a fan of reading either my phone or my computer but I decided to change that just during May and check out this book set in the Victorian era (the one I'm just studying right now in my career)...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464793689ra/19277621.gif" width="200" height="200/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464794188ra/19277728.gif" width="200" height="200/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So this is how I'm feeling right now.<br><br>The story follows Lilly Linton, a 19 year-old girl living in 1839 in London, a place where women have no political rights and are not allowed to vote or even to work. This strong girl tried (and failed) to vote for the first time dressing in men's clothes, and in the meantime he met him.<br>Mister Rikkard Ambrose.<br>Thinking she was a man, he offered her a job as his secretary... and for Lilly that means freedom.<br>Because she does NOT want to get married and have to depend on a man for her living. She is a proud suffragette and a feminist, and every time a man showed up in her life she hit min with her parasol.<br>The exception to that rule is Mr Ambrose, since she got the secretary post but for a price: she would have to dress up in men's clothes.<br>That man is like a combination of Mr Darcy and Christian Grey but waay meaner. The way he was bossing her around and not wanting to accept she was a girl has been driving me crazy for the last week. On another note, she created a lot of nicknames that went well with his personality and phisicaly form. These are my faves:<br><br> <i>Mr Cold Masculinity Ambrose<br>Mr Rich-and-Mysterious Ambrose<br>Mr Haughty Almighty and Annoyingly Handsome Ambrose<br>Mr Stoneface Ambrose<br>Mr Silent and Sullen Ambrose<br>Granite Face Ambrose<br>Mr Granite-Face All-Businesslike Ambrose<br>Mr Save-time-or-die Ambrose<br>Mr Arrogant-Stone-Face Ambrose <br>His Mightiness Mr Ambrose the Cold and Terrible</i><br><br>There are so many more and every single one made me laugh so much!!<br>The way Robert Thier wrote this amazing story had me in a cliffhanger after every single chapter. I loved Lilly's thoughts regarding love, secret affairs and very dangerous missions. She is definetly one of mu favourite female characters and I believe every single girl has an inner femminist in her mind.<br>Of course, my favourite parts were those where Mr Ambrose was present. I was reading all those parts like...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464804045ra/19279110.gif" width="200" height="200/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I mean, they were so romantic (well, not really, but they were for me) I was in awe all the time. He might be bossy but sometimes some very special moments might slip some time, specially when they were together searching for the stolen file and most of the credit went to her. Her sarcasm and thoughts were awesome every time and I felt so idetified with her because sometimes I behave like that. <u>(Warning: do not open the spoiler if you haven't read the book).</u> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>But why was it totally necessary to torture me for more than 300 pages to give me the most beautiful kiss I've ever read combined with Cassandra Clare's, E. L. James' and Jennifer Armentrout's way of writing kisses so then I had to stand for the last 200 pages that Mr Ambrose denied that beautiful moment ever happenned and that Lilly spent all the time wondering if that moment ever happenned or if it was just a dream? <b>WHYYYYYYY?????</b></i>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464804045ra/19279111.gif" width="200" height="200/" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>I finished the book last night in such a rush because I needed to know if they got the file, if they were able to escape from the evil's lair <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew from the very first moment it was Lord Dalgliesh the evil man behind all of it, never trust a man who knows how to fake a smile <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>and then the words THE END showed up with no head's up.<br>What?????<br>Why???<br>Why that horrible ending??? <br>I was staring at my phone with no emotions at all!!!!<br>And it's taken me three hours to write this review because it all hurts and because I had to run and find the second part so then I would be able to breath again!!!!!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464804045ra/19279112.gif" width="200" height="200/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464804045ra/19279113.gif" width="200" height="200/" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It's really hard to find such a story that didn't let me breathe while reading it but I think I have found it. I am now asking to all the world: <b>READ THIS NOW!!!! YOU WILL NOT REGRET IT!!!! </b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2902082173031976027" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1632349629">
  <td colspan="2">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520456682" />
    <a title="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5386619-nina-s"><img alt="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433066789p2/5386619.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520456682?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}" href="/user/show/5386619-nina-s">Nina {ᴡᴏʀᴅs ᴀɴᴅ ᴡᴀᴛᴇʀ}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5386619-nina-s?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>,
